<div class="cmpc">

<div class="byline">
  <div><div class="k">Author</div><div class="v">Inseong Paik</div></div>
  <div><div class="k">Published</div><div class="v">June 2026</div></div>
  <div><div class="k">Code</div><div class="v"><a href="https://github.com/ispaik06/convex-mpc-biped">github.com/ispaik06/convex-mpc-biped</a></div></div>
  <div><div class="k">Stack</div><div class="v">C++17 · MuJoCo · Eigen · OSQP · Python</div></div>
</div>

<figure class="hero-fig plain">
  <video autoplay loop muted playsinline preload="metadata" src="/assets/img/posts/convex-mpc/media/walk_full.mp4"></video>
  <figcaption><span class="figno">Video 1</span>The MIT Humanoid walking under the convex MPC
  in MuJoCo: omnidirectional velocity tracking, in-place turning, and body-pose tracking from
  a single controller and a single set of weights.</figcaption>
</figure>

<div class="abstract">
<span class="co-title">Abstract</span>
<p>
This article documents a locomotion controller I built for bipedal humanoid robots, centered on a
<strong>convex model-predictive controller (MPC)</strong> over <strong>single-rigid-body (SRB)</strong> dynamics.
The formulation follows the MIT Cheetah&nbsp;3 controller of Di&nbsp;Carlo et&nbsp;al., but a biped
is a harsher customer than a quadruped: there are only two contacts, the support region of each
foot is a small rectangle rather than a point, and single-support phases leave no margin for
sloppy force allocation. Moving from four point feet to two finite feet forces the decision
variable from 3D contact <em>forces</em> to 6D contact <em>wrenches</em>, and forces the constraint
set from a friction pyramid alone to a friction pyramid <em>plus</em> a center-of-pressure (CoP)
support polygon and a torsional friction bound — all expressed in each foot's yaw-rotated frame.
</p>
<p>
Beyond the QP itself, most of the engineering lives in the layers around it: a receding,
estimator-anchored reference trajectory that refuses to chase stale world-frame targets; a
body-yaw cost transform that keeps anisotropic tracking weights physically meaningful while
turning; a wrapped/unwrapped yaw policy that survives continuous rotation; Raibert-style
swing-foot planning with touchdown-yaw preview and capture-point stopping; early/late contact
handling that reconciles the gait schedule with measured contact; and OSQP solver engineering
(structure-exploiting sparsity, contact-signature cold starts, shifted warm starts) that keeps
the solve fast at 500&nbsp;Hz control rates. Every MPC solve can be captured as a self-contained
JSON snapshot and replayed offline through four independent verification layers. The result
walks, turns in place, and tracks body pose on the MIT Humanoid in MuJoCo, and retargets to the
Unitree G1 and H1 through robot-specific bindings and YAML tuning alone.
</p>
</div>

<ul class="contrib">
  <li><b>6D contact-wrench MPC with CoP constraints.</b> Full derivation of the rectangular
  support-polygon constraint for a yaw-rotated foot, from <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>x</mi><mrow><mi class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.1514em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.1389em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.044em;">z</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> to the
  sparse world-frame constraint matrix the solver actually touches.</li>
  <li><b>Frame discipline.</b> A deliberate split between world-frame dynamics, body-yaw command
  and cost semantics, and foot-frame contact geometry — including a convexity-preserving
  yaw-dependent cost transform and an unwrapped-yaw policy for the MPC state.</li>
  <li><b>Reactive contact management.</b> Hysteresis-based contact estimation, early-touchdown
  freezing, late-contact ground search, contact-force ramping, and a near-term MPC horizon
  override that keeps the QP consistent with measured contact.</li>
  <li><b>Solver engineering.</b> Row-level sparse constraint patterns, direct sparse fills without
  dense intermediates, contact-signature-triggered cold starts, and shifted warm starting.</li>
  <li><b>Reproducible debugging.</b> Single-keystroke MPC snapshots replayed through four
  verification layers: SRB reconstruction, wrench-realizability projection, a MuJoCo contact
  probe, and a full receding-horizon closed-loop replay.</li>
</ul>


<h2 id="introduction"><span class="secno">1</span>Introduction</h2>

<p>
Making a humanoid robot walk is a control problem with an unusually hostile structure.
Four properties conspire against you:
</p>

<ul>
  <li><strong>Floating-base dynamics.</strong> The torso is not bolted to anything. It moves
  freely in <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>S</mi><mi>E</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>3</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">SE(3)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0576em;">S</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0576em;">E</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">3</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span> and can only be stabilized indirectly, through whatever forces the feet can
  exert on the ground.</li>
  <li><strong>Underactuation.</strong> There is no actuator on the center of mass. During single
  support — most of a walking cycle — the system is fundamentally underactuated, and the
  controller must plan <em>through</em> the underactuation rather than fight it.</li>
  <li><strong>Hybrid contact dynamics.</strong> Every touchdown and liftoff switches the dynamics
  model. The controller must reason about a <em>sequence</em> of contact configurations, not a
  single smooth system.</li>
  <li><strong>A small support region.</strong> A quadruped in trot still spans a support line
  between diagonal feet; a biped in single support balances on one foot a few centimeters wide.
  Feasible contact wrenches live in a thin cone, and constraint violations turn directly into
  foot roll and falls.</li>
</ul>

<p>
Model-predictive control is a natural answer to the first three properties: predict the body
motion over a horizon that covers upcoming contact switches, and optimize contact forces subject
to the physics of friction. The catch has always been speed. Nonlinear whole-body MPC is
expensive and its solvers come with few guarantees; a controller that occasionally fails to
return a force is not a controller you can stand on.
</p>

<p>
The MIT Cheetah&nbsp;3 controller of <a href="#ref-dicarlo">Di&nbsp;Carlo et&nbsp;al. [1]</a>
showed how much of the problem survives aggressive simplification. Model the robot as a single
rigid body driven by ground-reaction forces; linearize the orientation dynamics around yaw;
treat the footstep locations as given by a heuristic planner. What remains is a <em>convex</em>
quadratic program that solves to global optimality in well under a millisecond — fast enough to
re-plan the entire force profile 25–50 times per second, robust enough to gallop a 45&nbsp;kg
quadruped at 3&nbsp;m/s.
</p>

<p>
This project asks: <em>how much of that story carries over to a biped, and what must be added
where it does not?</em> The answer occupies the rest of this article. The short version is that
the SRB-plus-convex-QP skeleton transfers beautifully, but essentially every interface around it
— the contact model, the constraint geometry, the reference generation, the cost frame, and the
recovery behaviors — has to be rebuilt for two feet.
</p>

<h3 id="from-quadruped-to-biped">1.1&ensp;From quadruped point feet to humanoid wrenches</h3>

<p>
The Cheetah's feet are rubber balls: each contact transmits a pure force, and the friction cone
is the entire constraint story. A humanoid foot is a rigid plate. It transmits a force
<em>and a moment</em> — a full 6D wrench — and that moment is bounded by the geometry of the
foot itself: push the center of pressure past the toe and the foot tips regardless of what the
QP believed. The table below summarizes what changed relative to the reference formulation.
</p>

<div class="tbl-wrap">
<table>
  <caption><span class="figno">Table 1</span>What transfers from the Cheetah&nbsp;3 formulation
  and what this project replaces.</caption>
  <thead>
    <tr><th>Aspect</th><th>Cheetah&nbsp;3 (Di&nbsp;Carlo et&nbsp;al.)</th><th>This project</th></tr>
  </thead>
  <tbody>
    <tr><td>Platform</td><td>Quadruped, 12 DoF</td><td>Biped humanoids (MIT Humanoid, Unitree G1/H1)</td></tr>
    <tr><td>Contact model</td><td>Point foot, 3D force <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi mathvariant="bold">f</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi><mn>3</mn></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{f}_i \in \mathbb{R}^3</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8444em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf" style="margin-right:0.109em;">f</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3117em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.109em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">i</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8141em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbb">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8141em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">3</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></td>
        <td>Finite foot, 6D wrench <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><msub><mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo separator="true">;</mo><mtext> </mtext><msub><mi mathvariant="bold">M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">]</mo><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi><mn>6</mn></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">[\mathbf{F}_i;\,\mathbf{M}_i] \in \mathbb{R}^6</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">[</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">F</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3117em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">i</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mpunct">;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">M</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3117em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">i</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose">]</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8141em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbb">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8141em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">6</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></td></tr>
    <tr><td>Input dimension / step</td><td><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>3</mn><mi>n</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">3n</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">3</span><span class="mord mathnormal">n</span></span></span></span>, up to 4 contacts</td><td><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>12</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">12</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">12</span></span></span></span> (two feet, forces + moments)</td></tr>
    <tr><td>Force constraints</td><td>Friction pyramid, <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>F</mi><mi>z</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">F_z</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8333em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">F</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.1514em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.1389em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.044em;">z</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> bounds</td>
        <td>Friction pyramid, <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>F</mi><mi>z</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">F_z</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8333em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">F</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.1514em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.1389em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.044em;">z</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> bounds, <b>rectangular CoP polygon</b>, <b>torsional friction</b>, all in the yaw-rotated foot frame</td></tr>
    <tr><td>Swing-leg DoF handling</td><td>3-DoF legs, full task-space control</td>
        <td>5-DoF legs (MIT) require a no-roll-moment equality row and wrench-realizability analysis; 6-DoF legs (G1) use the full wrench</td></tr>
    <tr><td>Cost frame</td><td>World-axis diagonal weights</td>
        <td>Body-yaw-rotated tracking cost, fixed from the reference yaw to preserve convexity</td></tr>
    <tr><td>Reference</td><td>Operator velocities integrated forward</td>
        <td>Estimator-anchored receding reference with gait-gated yaw integration</td></tr>
    <tr><td>QP solver</td><td>qpOASES, dense</td><td>OSQP via OsqpEigen, structure-exploiting sparsity, signature-aware warm starts</td></tr>
  </tbody>
</table>
</div>

<h3 id="scope">1.2&ensp;Scope and honest framing</h3>

<p>
Everything here runs in MuJoCo with ground-truth (“cheater”) state estimation; hardware transfer,
sensor-based estimation, and rough terrain are explicitly out of scope
(<a href="#limitations">§14</a>). The MIT Humanoid is the primary, validated platform — its MJCF
is not redistributed in the public repository — and the Unitree G1/H1 configurations are
integration starting points rather than tuned results. The project was built over roughly three
months as a from-scratch implementation: the simulator harness, controller stack, solver
integration, debugging tools, and the web telemetry dashboard are all part of the codebase this
article walks through.
</p>

<div class="callout">
<span class="co-title">How to read this article</span>
<p>
Sections <a href="#architecture">2</a>–<a href="#srb-model">3</a> set up the architecture and the
model. Sections <a href="#convex-mpc">4</a>–<a href="#constraints">5</a> are the mathematical
core: the condensed QP and the contact-wrench constraint set. Sections
<a href="#reference-trajectory">6</a>–<a href="#torque">9</a> cover the planning and execution
layers around the QP. Sections <a href="#solver">10</a>–<a href="#debugging">12</a> are the
systems half: solver engineering, robot-independent structure, and the debugging methodology.
Results and limitations close it out. Readers who want the biped-specific mathematics can go
straight to <a href="#constraints">§5</a>.
</p>
</div>


<h2 id="architecture"><span class="secno">2</span>System Architecture</h2>

<p>
The controller is organized as a strict hierarchy — <em>planning decides, prediction optimizes,
execution obeys</em> — with one non-negotiable invariant: every layer consumes the same contact
schedule and the same motion reference. Most walking-controller bugs I encountered were not bugs
inside a layer but disagreements <em>between</em> layers about who is in contact and where the
body is supposed to be; the architecture exists to make such disagreements structurally hard to
write.
</p>

<figure class="diagram" role="img" aria-label="Three-layer control hierarchy diagram">
<svg viewBox="0 0 860 470" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">

    </marker>

<figcaption><span class="figno">Figure 1</span>The three-layer control hierarchy. The
<code>ContactManager</code> sits between planning and prediction as a reactive overlay: it can
override both the swing-foot targets and the near-term MPC contact schedule when measured
contact disagrees with the nominal gait (<a href="#gait">§7</a>).</figcaption>
</figure>

<h3 id="runtime-loop">2.1&ensp;Runtime loop</h3>

<p>
One process runs everything. <code>SimulationRunner</code> owns the MuJoCo model and steps
physics at 500&nbsp;Hz; on every step it refreshes the cheater-state estimate, runs
<code>RobotRunner</code> — which drives leg/arm initialization and then the controller proper —
and applies the composed torque command back to the actuators. Inside
<code>MyController::runController()</code> the per-tick sequence is fixed:
</p>

<ol>
  <li>synchronize the <code>LocomotionFSM</code> and the horizon clock;</li>
  <li>filter the user command and update the body pose target;</li>
  <li>query the <code>SwingFootPlanner</code> for nominal touchdown targets;</li>
  <li>let the <code>ContactManager</code> reconcile scheduled vs. measured contact and possibly
      override those targets;</li>
  <li>advance the swing trajectories;</li>
  <li>if this tick is a scheduled solve boundary: rebuild reference, SRB matrices, constraints,
      and solve the QP;</li>
  <li>write leg commands — stance legs get the newest optimal wrench, swing legs get
      trajectory-tracking commands.</li>
</ol>

<div class="tbl-wrap">
<table class="tbl-num">
  <caption><span class="figno">Table 2</span>Execution rates in the current MIT Humanoid tuning.
  All timing is YAML-driven; the MPC solve cadence is <code>iterations_between_solve = 7</code>
  control ticks.</caption>
  <thead><tr><th>Layer</th><th>Rate</th><th>Period</th></tr></thead>
  <tbody>
    <tr><td>MuJoCo physics integration</td><td>500 Hz</td><td>2 ms</td></tr>
    <tr><td>State estimation + controller tick</td><td>500 Hz</td><td>2 ms</td></tr>
    <tr><td>Contact management + swing update</td><td>500 Hz</td><td>2 ms</td></tr>
    <tr><td>Leg / arm torque generation</td><td>500 Hz</td><td>2 ms</td></tr>
    <tr><td>MPC solve + reference rebuild</td><td>≈71.4 Hz</td><td>14 ms</td></tr>
    <tr><td>MPC prediction grid (<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi>t</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\Delta t</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">Δ</span><span class="mord mathnormal">t</span></span></span></span>, horizon <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">=</mo><mn>25</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">H{=}25</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mord"><span class="mrel">=</span></span><span class="mord">25</span></span></span></span>)</td><td>50 Hz</td><td>20 ms × 25 = 0.5 s</td></tr>
  </tbody>
</table>
</div>

<div class="callout">
<span class="co-title">Design note — two clocks, deliberately decoupled</span>
<p>
The solve cadence (every 7 ticks, 14&nbsp;ms) and the prediction grid (20&nbsp;ms) are
intentionally different knobs. The horizon spacing is tied to the gait — 25 samples at 20&nbsp;ms
cover exactly one 0.5&nbsp;s gait cycle — while the solve rate is tuned to how quickly the robot
must react to disturbances. A <code>HorizonClock</code> keeps the horizon sample times anchored
to a consistent cycle origin so that gait phase, constraint schedule, and reference all agree on
what time step <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0315em;">k</span></span></span></span> means.
</p>
</div>


<h2 id="srb-model"><span class="secno">3</span>The Single-Rigid-Body Model and Frame Conventions</h2>

<p>
The predictive model deliberately forgets that the robot has legs. It sees one rigid body — the
torso, carrying the full mass and a fixed body-frame inertia — acted on by gravity and by a
contact wrench at each foot. For the Cheetah this approximation was justified by light legs
(≈10% of total mass); a humanoid's legs are heavier, and part of this project's debugging
apparatus (<a href="#debugging">§12</a>) exists precisely to measure how far reality drifts from
this model before the controller stops being able to hide the difference.
</p>

<h3 id="state-input">3.1&ensp;State and input</h3>

<p>The MPC state is the 13-vector</p>

<div class="eq"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="bold">x</mi><mtext>  </mtext><mo>=</mo><mtext>  </mtext><msup><mrow><mo fence="true">[</mo><mtable rowspacing="0.16em" columnalign="center center center center center center center center center center center center center" columnspacing="1em"><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mi>ϕ</mi></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mi>θ</mi></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mi>ψ</mi></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>x</mi></msub></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>y</mi></msub></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>z</mi></msub></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><msub><mi>ω</mi><mi>x</mi></msub></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><msub><mi>ω</mi><mi>y</mi></msub></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><msub><mi>ω</mi><mi>z</mi></msub></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><msub><mi>v</mi><mi>x</mi></msub></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><msub><mi>v</mi><mi>y</mi></msub></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><msub><mi>v</mi><mi>z</mi></msub></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mi>g</mi></mstyle></mtd></mtr></mtable><mo fence="true">]</mo></mrow><mrow><mtext> ⁣</mtext><mi mathvariant="normal">⊤</mi></mrow></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{x} \;=\;
\begin{bmatrix}
\phi &amp; \theta &amp; \psi &amp;
p_x &amp; p_y &amp; p_z &amp;
\omega_x &amp; \omega_y &amp; \omega_z &amp;
v_x &amp; v_y &amp; v_z &amp;
g
\end{bmatrix}^{\!\top}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4444em;"></span><span class="mord — Z-Y-X Euler orientation <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="bold">Θ</mi><mo>=</mo><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mi>ϕ</mi><mtext>  </mtext><mi>θ</mi><mtext>  </mtext><mi>ψ</mi><msup><mo stretchy="false">]</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⊤</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\boldsymbol{\Theta} = [\phi\;\theta\;\psi]^\top</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6861em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">Θ</span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.0991em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">[</span><span class="mord mathnormal">ϕ</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">θ</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">ψ</span><span class="mclose"><span class="mclose">]</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8491em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">⊤</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> (roll, pitch, yaw),
COM position <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi mathvariant="bold">p</mi><mi>W</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{p}^W</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.0358em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">p</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8413em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>, angular velocity <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">ω</mi><mi>W</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\boldsymbol{\omega}^W</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8413em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord boldsymbol" style="margin-right:0.037em;">ω</span></span></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8413em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>, COM velocity
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi mathvariant="bold">v</mi><mi>W</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{v}^W</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8413em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf" style="margin-right:0.016em;">v</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8413em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>, and a constant gravity state <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>g</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">g</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.625em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">g</span></span></span></span> appended so that gravity enters the dynamics as
part of a homogeneous linear system rather than as an affine offset. The input stacks both feet's
wrenches, forces first:
</p>

style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mspace mtight" style="margin-right:-0.1952em;"></span><span class="mord mtight">⊤</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord"> per foot.</span></span></span></span></span></span></div>

<div class="callout warn">
<span class="co-title">Convention that will matter later</span>
<p>
Each foot's moment <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi mathvariant="bold">M</mi><mi>W</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{M}^W</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8413em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">M</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8413em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> is expressed in world axes but taken <em>about that foot's
contact-frame origin</em>, not about the COM. The CoP constraints of <a href="#constraints">§5</a>
and the torque mapping of <a href="#torque">§9</a> are only consistent because both respect this
reference point; mixing it up produces wrenches that look feasible to the QP and tip the foot in
simulation. The debugging contact probe (<a href="#debugging">§12.3</a>) measures its realized
moment about this same point for exactly this reason.
</p>
</div>

<h3 id="frames">3.2&ensp;The three-frame split</h3>

<p>
Three frames appear throughout the controller, and the discipline about <em>which quantity lives
where</em> is one of the central design decisions of the project:
</p>

<div class="tbl-wrap">
<table>
  <caption><span class="figno">Table 3</span>Frame assignment. World for dynamics and geometry,
  body-yaw for meaning, foot for contact feasibility.</caption>
  <thead><tr><th>Frame</th><th>Symbol</th><th>What lives here</th></tr></thead>
  <tbody>
    <tr><td>World</td><td><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>W</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">W</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span></span></span></span></td><td>SRB dynamics, COM state, touchdown positions, MPC wrench
    decision variables, debug markers</td></tr>
    <tr><td>Body-yaw</td><td><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>B</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">B</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span></span></span></span></td><td>User command semantics, nominal foot offsets,
    capture-point braking offsets, the <em>meaning</em> of planar tracking costs</td></tr>
    <tr><td>Foot</td><td><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>F</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">F</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">F</span></span></span></span></td><td>Friction pyramid, rectangular CoP region, torsional
    friction limit</td></tr>
  </tbody>
</table>
</div>

<p>
The body-yaw frame is a bookkeeping frame, not a full 6-DoF body frame: it shares the world's
vertical axis and only rotates by the yaw <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>ψ</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\psi</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8889em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">ψ</span></span></span></span>. Commands transform into the world frame
through
</p>

<div class="eq"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><msubsup><mi mathvariant="bold">v</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi></mrow><mi>W</mi></msubsup><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>R</mi><mi>z</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>ψ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mtext> </mtext><msubsup><mi mathvariant="bold">v</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi></mrow><mi>B</mi></msubsup><mo separator="true">,</mo><mspace width="2em"/><msub><mi>R</mi><mi>z</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>ψ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo fence="true">[</mo><mtable rowspacing="0.16em" columnalign="center center center" columnspacing="1em"><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mi>cos</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mi>ψ</mi></mrow></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mo>−</mo><mi>sin</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mi>ψ</mi></mrow></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mn>0</mn></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mi>sin</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mi>ψ</mi></mrow></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mi>cos</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mi>ψ</mi></mrow></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mn>0</mn></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mn>0</mn></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mn>0</mn></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mn>1</mn></mstyle></mtd></mtr></mtable><mo fence="true">]</mo></mrow><mo separator="true">,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{v}^{W}_{\mathrm{cmd}} = R_z(\psi)\, \mathbf{v}^{B}_{\mathrm{cmd}},
\qquad
R_z(\psi) =
\begin{bmatrix}
\cos\psi &amp; -\sin\psi &amp; 0\\
\sin\psi &amp; \cos\psi &amp; 0\\
0 &amp; 0 &amp; 1
\end{bmatrix},</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.1383em;vertical-align:-0.247em;"></span><span style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">ψ</span></span></span><span style="top:-1.81em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:1.55em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="arraycolsep" style="width:0.5em;"></span><span <p>
foot-frame contact quantities relate to the world through the foot yaw <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>ψ</mi><mi>F</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\psi_F</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8889em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">ψ</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3283em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.0359em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">F</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>,
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi><mi>F</mi></msup><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>R</mi><mi>z</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>ψ</mi><mi>F</mi></msub><msup><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⊤</mi></msup><msup><mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi><mi>W</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{F}^F = R_z(\psi_F)^\top \mathbf{F}^W</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8413em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">F</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8413em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">F</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.0991em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0077em;">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.1514em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.0077em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.044em;">z</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">ψ</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3283em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.0359em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">F</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose"><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8491em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">⊤</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">F</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8413em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> (and identically for moments), and the tracking
error is weighted in a frame rotated by the <em>reference</em> yaw
(<a href="#cost-transform">§4.3</a>). Keeping only yaw — never roll or pitch — in these
transforms avoids mixing tilt into the vertical axis of a reduced model that has no business
reasoning about tilted support surfaces.
</p>

<h3 id="orientation-dynamics">3.3&ensp;Linearized orientation kinematics</h3>

<p>
The exact relation between Euler-angle rates and world angular velocity, for Z-Y-X angles and
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>cos</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo mathvariant="normal">≠</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\cos\theta \neq 0</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8889em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mop">cos</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">θ</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel"><span class="mrel"><span class="mord vbox"><span class="thinbox"><span class="rlap"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8889em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="inner"><span class="mord"><span class="mrel"></span></span></span><span class="fix"></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace nobreak"></span><span class="mrel">=</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">0</span></span></span></span>, is
</p>

<div class="eq"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mo fence="true">]</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo fence="true">[</mo><mtable rowspacing="0.16em" columnalign="center center center" columnspacing="1em"><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mn>0</mn></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mo>−</mo><mi>sin</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mi>ψ</mi></mrow></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mi>cos</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mi>ψ</mi></mrow></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mn>0</mn></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mi>cos</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mi>ψ</mi><mi>tan</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mi>θ</mi></mrow></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" encoding="application/x-tex">\begin{bmatrix} \dot\phi \\ \dot\theta \\ \dot\psi \end{bmatrix}
=
\begin{bmatrix}
\cos\psi/\cos\theta &amp; \sin\psi/\cos\theta &amp; 0\\
-\sin\psi &amp; \cos\psi &amp; 0\\
\cos\psi\tan\theta &amp; \sin\psi\tan\theta &amp; 1
\end{bmatrix}
\boldsymbol{\omega}^W .</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:3.8739em;vertical-align:-1.687em;"></span><span class="minner"><span class="mopen"><span class="delimsizing mult"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:2.05em;"><span style="top:-4.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:5.6em;"></span><span style="width:0.667em;height:3.6em;"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="0.667em" height="3.6em" viewBox="0 0 667 3600"><path d="M403 1759 V84 H666 V0 H319 V1759 v0 v1759 v84 h347 v-84

<p>
For walking, roll and pitch stay near zero — the reference holds them at the pose target, and the
weights of <a href="#results">Table&nbsp;7</a> punish deviations hard — so the small-angle form
is used, which is exact in yaw and first-order in tilt:
</p>

<div class="eq"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi mathvariant="normal">⊤</mi></msup><msup><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">ω</mi><mi>W</mi></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">.</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\dot{\boldsymbol{\Theta}} \;\approx\; R_z(\psi)^\top \boldsymbol{\omega}^W .</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0077em;">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.1514em;"><span mtight" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord">.</span></span></span></span></span></div>

<p>
Similarly, the rotational dynamics
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle scriptlevel="0" drop the gyroscopic term <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">ω</mi><mo>×</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi mathvariant="bold">I</mi><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">ω</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\boldsymbol{\omega} \times (\mathbf{I}\boldsymbol{\omega})</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6667em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord boldsymbol" style="margin-right:0.037em;">ω</span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathbf">I</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord boldsymbol" style="margin-right:0.037em;">ω</span></span></span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span> — small at
humanoid walking speeds — and use the <strong>yaw-rotated inertia</strong>
</p>

<div class="eq"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi mathvariant="normal">⊤</mi></mrow></msup><mo separator="true">,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\hat{\mathbf{I}}(\psi) \;=\; R_z(\psi)\, {}^{B}\!\mathbf{I}\, R_z(\psi)^{\!\top},</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.1995em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord accent"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.9495em;"><span style="top:-3em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord mathbf">I</span></span><span style="top:-3.2551em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="accent-body" class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.1491em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0077em;">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.1514em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.0077em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">ψ</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8913em;"><span style="top:-3.113em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0077em;">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.1514em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.0077em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.044em;">z</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">ψ</span><span class="mclose"><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8991em;"><span style="top:-3.113em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mspace mtight" style="margin-right:-0.1952em;"></span><span class="mord mtight">⊤</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mpunct">,</span></span></span></span></span></div>

<p>
which is the world-frame inertia of the body-frame tensor <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mrow></mrow><mi>B</mi></msup><mi mathvariant="bold">I</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{}^{B}\mathbf{I}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8413em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8413em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathbf">I</span></span></span></span> under the
small-tilt assumption. Both approximations are inherited from [1]; what is <em>not</em> inherited
is where <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>ψ</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\psi</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8889em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">ψ</span></span></span></span> comes from — each horizon step <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0315em;">k</span></span></span></span> uses its own reference yaw <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>ψ</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\psi_k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8889em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">ψ</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3361em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.0359em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0315em;">k</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>
(<a href="#convex-mpc">§4</a>), which is what lets the same QP remain honest during sustained
in-place turning at 1.3&nbsp;rad/s.
</p>

<h3 id="continuous-dynamics">3.4&ensp;Continuous-time model</h3>

<p>
Assembling the pieces, with foot lever arms <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi><mi>L</mi></msub><mo separator="true">,</mo><msub><mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi><mi>R</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{r}_L, \mathbf{r}_R</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6389em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">r</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3283em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">L</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">r</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3283em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0077em;">R</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> (foot position minus
reference body position, <a href="#reference-trajectory">§6.4</a>) and mass <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span>:
</p>

<div class="eq"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi mathvariant="bold">x</mi><mo>˙</mo></mover><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>A</mi><mi>c</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>ψ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mtext> </mtext><mi mathvariant="bold">x</mi><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>B</mi><mi>c</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi><mi>L</mi></msub><mo separator="true">,</mo><msub><mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi><mi>R</mi></msub><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>ψ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mtext> </mtext><mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi><mo separator="true">,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\dot{\mathbf{x}} = A_c(\psi)\,\mathbf{x} + B_c(\mathbf{r}_L, \mathbf{r}_R, \psi)\,\mathbf{u},</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6813em;"></span><span class="mord accent"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.6813em;"><span style="top:-3em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord mathbf">x</span></span><span style="top:-3.0134em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="accent-body" style="left:-0.1389em;"><span class="mord">˙</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="top:-4.2648em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3011em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">3</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" class="mord"><span class="mord accent"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.9495em;"><span style="top:-3em;"><span class="pstrut" class="mord">^</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8141em;"><span style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3011em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">3</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="top:-0.5552em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord M347 1759 V0 H263 V1759 v2400 v1759 h84z"/></svg></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:2.75em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.0585em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbb">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8641em;"><span style="top:-3.113em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">13</span><span class="mbin mtight">×</span><span class="mord mtight">12</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mpunct">,</span></span></span></span></span></div>

<p>
where <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi><msub><mo stretchy="false">]</mo><mo>×</mo></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">[\mathbf{r}]_\times</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">[</span><span class="mord mathbf">r</span><span class="mclose"><span class="mclose">]</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.2583em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mbin mtight">×</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.2083em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> is the skew-symmetric cross-product matrix and <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi mathvariant="bold">e</mi><mi>z</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{e}_z</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.5944em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">e</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.1514em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.044em;">z</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> routes
the gravity state into <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>v</mi><mo>˙</mo></mover><mi>z</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\dot{v}_z</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8179em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord accent"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.6679em;"><span style="top:-3em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">v</span></span><span style="top:-3em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="accent-body" style="left:-0.1111em;"><span class="mord">˙</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.1514em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.0359em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.044em;">z</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>. The two right-hand block columns of <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>B</mi><mi>c</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">B_c</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8333em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.1514em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.0502em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">c</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> are the humanoid
extension in its most compact form: <strong>foot moments act on the body directly through
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mover accent="true"><mi mathvariant="bold">I</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\hat{\mathbf{I}}^{-1}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.9495em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord accent"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.9495em;"><span style="top:-3em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord mathbf">I</span></span><span style="top:-3.2551em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="accent-body" style="left:-0.25em;"><span class="mord">^</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8141em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">−</span><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></strong>, independent of the lever arms. This is what gives a biped in
single support its authority over roll and pitch — and it is exactly the channel that the CoP
constraints of <a href="#constraints">§5</a> must keep physically honest, because the model
itself would happily request a moment the foot cannot deliver.
</p>

<p>
Given yaw and lever arms along the reference trajectory, <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>A</mi><mi>c</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">A_c</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8333em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.1514em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">c</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>B</mi><mi>c</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">B_c</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8333em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.1514em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.0502em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">c</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> are known
<em>functions of time step</em>, not of the decision variables — the dynamics become linear
time-varying, and the MPC stays convex.
</p>


<h2 id="convex-mpc"><span class="secno">4</span>The Convex MPC: Discretization, Condensing, and Cost Geometry</h2>

<h3 id="discretization">4.1&ensp;Zero-order-hold discretization</h3>

<p>
Each horizon step <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0315em;">k</span></span></span></span> carries its own continuous-time pair <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>A</mi><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>k</mi></mrow></msub><mo separator="true">,</mo><msub><mi>B</mi><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>k</mi></mrow></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(A_{c,k}, B_{c,k})</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.0361em;vertical-align:-0.2861em;"></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3361em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">c</span><span class="mpunct mtight">,</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0315em;">k</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.2861em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3361em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.0502em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">c</span><span class="mpunct mtight">,</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0315em;">k</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.2861em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span>, built from the
reference yaw <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>ψ</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\psi_k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8889em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">ψ</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3361em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.0359em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0315em;">k</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and the reference lever arms <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi><mrow><mi>L</mi><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>k</mi></mrow></msub><mo separator="true">,</mo><msub><mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>k</mi></mrow></msub></mrow><annotation
